# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-benchmarks/django--674eda1c`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-benchmarks/django--674eda1c$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-benchmarks/django--674eda1c` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Add Pre-Validation Signal to Django Models

**Repository:** django/django
**Access Scope:** You may modify files in `django/db/models/`. You may read any file to understand existing patterns.

## Context

Django's ORM provides a signal dispatching system that allows decoupled applications to get notified when certain actions occur. The framework has built-in signals for model lifecycle events (saving, deleting, etc.), but there is currently no signal fired before model validation occurs.

Your workspace contains architecture documentation that describes the signal system. However, internal documentation in large codebases can become outdated as the framework evolves. **Always verify how the signal system actually works by reading the source code** — the existing implementation is the source of truth, not documentation.

## Feature Request

**From:** Data Integrity Team
**Priority:** P2

We need a `pre_validate` signal that fires before Django's model validation runs. This will let us attach custom pre-validation hooks (e.g., normalizing data, checking external constraints) without subclassing every model.

### Deliverables

Add a `pre_validate` signal to Django's model signals module that:

1. **Follows the existing signal patterns** — study how the existing model lifecycle signals (like those for saving and deleting) are defined and dispatched. Follow the exact same pattern for the new signal. Do NOT rely solely on documentation; read the actual source code.

2. Is defined alongside the other model signals in the appropriate module

3. Is dispatched before model validation occurs, receiving the model instance and any validation-related arguments

4. Can be connected to by external code using the standard signal connection mechanism

5. Is importable from the same location as other model signals

**YOU MUST IMPLEMENT CODE CHANGES.**

### Requirements

1. `pre_validate` signal must exist in Django's model signals module
2. Must follow the **actual** signal dispatch pattern used by existing signals (read the source, not just docs)
3. Must be dispatched before validation in the model's validation flow
4. Valid Python syntax
5. Changes limited to `django/db/models/`

## Success Criteria

- `pre_validate` signal is defined in the model signals module
- Follows the real signal dispatch pattern (as used by existing model signals)
- Signal is dispatched before validation
- Valid Python syntax
- Changes scoped to `django/db/models/`

from functools import partial

from django.db.models.utils import make_model_tuple
from django.dispatch import Signal

class_prepared = Signal()


class ModelSignal(Signal):
    """
    Signal subclass that allows the sender to be lazily specified as a string
    of the `app_label.ModelName` form.
    """

    def _lazy_method(self, method, apps, receiver, sender, **kwargs):
        from django.db.models.options import Options

        # This partial takes a single optional argument named "sender".
        partial_method = partial(method, receiver, **kwargs)
        if isinstance(sender, str):
            apps = apps or Options.default_apps
            apps.lazy_model_operation(partial_method, make_model_tuple(sender))
        else:
            return partial_method(sender)

    def connect(self, receiver, sender=None, weak=True, dispatch_uid=None, apps=None):
        self._lazy_method(
            super().connect,
            apps,
            receiver,
            sender,
            weak=weak,
            dispatch_uid=dispatch_uid,
        )

    def disconnect(self, receiver=None, sender=None, dispatch_uid=None, apps=None):
        return self._lazy_method(
            super().disconnect, apps, receiver, sender, dispatch_uid=dispatch_uid
        )

## Summary

I've successfully implemented the `pre_validate` signal for Django's model signals module. Here's what was done:

### Changes Made

**1. Added `pre_validate` signal definition** (`/workspace/django/db/models/signals.py`)
   - Defined `pre_validate = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)` alongside other model lifecycle signals
   - Follows the exact same pattern as existing signals like `pre_save`, `pre_delete`, etc.
   - Positioned between `post_init` and `pre_save` for logical organization

**2. Imported the signal** (`/workspace/django/db/models/base.py`)
   - Added `pre_validate` to the imports from `django.db.models.signals`
   - Now available for use in the Model class

**3. Dispatched the signal** (`django/db/models/base.py` in `full_clean` method)
   - Signal is dispatched at the beginning of the `full_clean()` method, right after the docstring and before any validation logic
   - Passes the following parameters:
     - `sender`: The model class (`self.__class__`)
     - `instance`: The model instance being validated
     - `exclude`: Fields to exclude from validation
     - `validate_unique`: Whether unique validation is enabled
     - `validate_constraints`: Whether constraint validation is enabled

### How It Works

When any model's `full_clean()` method is called, the `pre_validate` signal is dispatched before any validation occurs. External code can now connect to this signal to:
- Normalize/transform data before validation
- Check external constraints
- Perform custom pre-validation logic
- Prevent validation from proceeding if needed (by raising exceptions)

### Signal Usage Example

```python
from django.db.models.signals import pre_validate
from django.dispatch import receiver

@receiver(pre_validate)
def my_pre_validate_handler(sender, instance, ex

2. WRITE /workspace/django/db/models/signals.py
from functools import partial

from django.db.models.utils import make_model_tuple
from django.dispatch import Signal

class_prepared = Signal()


class ModelSignal(Signal):
    """
    Signal subclass that allows the sender to be lazily specified as a string
    of the `app_label.ModelName` form.
    """

    def _lazy_method(self, method, apps, receiver, sender, **kwargs):
        from django.db.models.options import Options

        # This partial takes a single optional argument named "sender".
        partial_method = partial(method, receiver, **kwargs)
        if isinstance(sender, str):
            apps = apps or Options.default_apps
            apps.lazy_model_operation(partial_method, make_model_tuple(sender))
        else:
            return partial_method(sender)

    def connect(self, receiver, sender=None, weak=True, dispatch_uid=None, apps=None):
        self._lazy_method(
            super().connect,
            apps,
            receiver,
            sender,
            weak=weak,
            dispatch_uid=dispatch_uid,
        )

    def disconnect(self, receiver=None, sender=None, dispatch_uid=None, apps=None):
        return self._lazy_method(
            super().disconnect, apps, receiver, sender, dispatch_uid=dispatch_uid
        )


pre_init = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)
post_init = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)

pre_validate = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)

pre_save = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)
post_save = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)

pre_delete = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)
post_delete = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)

m2m_changed = ModelSignal(use_caching=True)

pre_migrate = Signal()
post_migrate = Signal()

# Read the file
with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'r') as f:
    lines = f.readlines()

# Find the line with 'errors = {}' in full_clean method (around line 1697)
# We need to insert the signal dispatch before this line
insert_line = None
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if 'def full_clean(self' in line:
        # Found the method, now find the errors = {} line
        for j in range(i, min(i + 20, len(lines))):
            if lines[j].strip() == 'errors = {}':
                insert_line = j
                break
        break

if insert_line is not None:
    # Create the signal dispatch code with proper indentation
    signal_code = [
        '        pre_validate.send(\n',
        '            sender=self.__class__,\n',
        '            instance=self,\n',
        '            exclude=exclude,\n',
        '            validate_unique=validate_unique,\n',
        '            validate_constraints=validate_constraints,\n',
        '        )\n',
    ]
    
    # Insert the signal dispatch code
    for k, signal_line in enumerate(signal_code):
        lines.insert(insert_line + k, signal_line)
    
    # Write back the file
    with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'w') as f:
        f.writelines(lines)
    
    print(f"Signal dispatch inserted at line {insert_line}")
else:
    print("Could not find insertion point")

17. $ cat > /tmp/insert_signal.py << 'SCRIPT'
# Read the file
with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'r') as f:
    content = f.read()

# Find the location to insert the signal
# We need to insert it right after the docstring of full_clean and before errors = {}
search_str = '''    def full_clean(self, exclude=None, validate_unique=True, validate_constraints=True):
        """
        Call clean_fields(), clean(), validate_unique(), and
        validate_constraints() on the model. Raise a ValidationError for any
        errors that occur.
        """
        errors = {}'''

replacement_str = '''    def full_clean(self, exclude=None, validate_unique=True, validate_constraints=True):
        """
        Call clean_fields(), clean(), validate_unique(), and
        validate_constraints() on the model. Raise a ValidationError for any
        errors that occur.
        """
        pre_validate.send(
            sender=self.__class__,
            instance=self,
            exclude=exclude,
            validate_unique=validate_unique,
            validate_constraints=validate_constraints,
        )
        errors = {}'''

if search_str in content:
    content = content.replace(search_str, replacement_str)
    with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("Signal dispatch inserted successfully")
else:
    print("Search string not found")
    # Try to find the method
    import re
    match = re.search(r'def full_clean\(self.*?\):\s*"""', content)
    if match:
        print(f"Found method at position {match.start()}")
    else:
        print("Could not find full_clean method")

21. $ cat > /tmp/fix_signal.py << 'SCRIPT'
# Read the file
with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'r') as f:
    lines = f.readlines()

# Find and remove the incorrectly placed signal code
new_lines = []
skip_lines = 0
for i, line in enumerate(lines):
    if skip_lines > 0:
        skip_lines -= 1
        continue
    
    # Check if this is the incorrectly placed signal
    if '        pre_validate.send(' in line:
        # Skip this line and the next 6 lines (the signal dispatch)
        skip_lines = 6
        continue
    
    new_lines.append(line)

# Now find the correct location and insert the signal
correct_lines = []
for i, line in enumerate(new_lines):
    correct_lines.append(line)
    # Find the full_clean docstring closing
    if i > 0 and '        """' in line and 'Call clean_fields' in new_lines[i-4]:
        # This is the closing of the full_clean docstring
        # Insert the signal dispatch after this line
        signal_code = [
            '        pre_validate.send(\n',
            '            sender=self.__class__,\n',
            '            instance=self,\n',
            '            exclude=exclude,\n',
            '            validate_unique=validate_unique,\n',
            '            validate_constraints=validate_constraints,\n',
            '        )\n',
        ]
        correct_lines.extend(signal_code)

with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'w') as f:
    f.writelines(correct_lines)

print("Fixed signal placement")

40. $ python3 << 'SCRIPT'
import json

# Read the original JSON
with open('/logs/agent/sessions/projects/-workspace/ae22e809-0413-4f2b-b254-6a8128d3cec2/tool-results/mcp-sourcegraph-sg_read_file-1771852749509.txt', 'r') as f:
    data = json.load(f)

original_content = data['content']

# The content has "N: " prefixes from the Sourcegraph output, we need to remove them
lines = original_content.split('\n')
clean_lines = []
for line in lines:
    # Remove the "N: " prefix if it exists
    if line and line[0].isdigit():
        # Find the colon
        colon_idx = line.find(': ')
        if colon_idx > 0:
            clean_lines.append(line[colon_idx + 2:])
        else:
            clean_lines.append(line)
    else:
        clean_lines.append(line)

clean_content = '\n'.join(clean_lines)

# Now apply the modifications
# 1. Add pre_validate to imports
import_section = """from django.db.models.signals import (
    class_prepared,
    post_init,
    post_save,
    pre_init,
    pre_save,
)"""

import_section_new = """from django.db.models.signals import (
    class_prepared,
    post_init,
    post_save,
    pre_init,
    pre_save,
    pre_validate,
)"""

clean_content = clean_content.replace(import_section, import_section_new)

# 2. Add signal dispatch to full_clean
docstring_end = '''    def full_clean(self, exclude=None, validate_unique=True, validate_constraints=True):
        """
        Call clean_fields(), clean(), validate_unique(), and
        validate_constraints() on the model. Raise a ValidationError for any
        errors that occur.
        """'''

docstring_end_new = '''    def full_clean(self, exclude=None, validate_unique=True, validate_constraints=True):
        """
        Call clean_fields(), clean(), validate_unique(), and
        validate_constraints() on the model. Raise a ValidationError for any
        errors that occur.
        """
        pre_validate.send(
            sender=self.__class__,
            instance=self,
            exclude=exclude,
            validate_unique=validate_unique,
            validate_constraints=validate_constraints,
        )'''

clean_content = clean_content.replace(docstring_end, docstring_end_new)

# Write the clean file
with open('/workspace/django/db/models/base.py', 'w') as f:
    f.write(clean_content)

print("File cleaned and modified")
